## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task seeks the rate law dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. In chemical kinetics, the rate of change of a reactant's concentration is governed by rate laws that typically depend on powers of concentration, and sometimes on time explicitly for non-autonomous systems.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (generalized power-law rate)
- Mixed order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (power-law rate with constant production/consumption)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order decay with back-reaction equilibrium)
- Second-order with first-order competing: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A (parallel reaction pathways)
- Autocatalytic rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (rate with substrate inhibition)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant)
- Cubic kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 + c1 * A (third-order with first-order term)
- Rational rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (saturation kinetics for single species)
- Square root kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (half-order kinetics, surface reactions)
- Polynomial rate: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 + c1 * A**2 + c2 * A + c3 (general polynomial in concentration)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate with power-law concentration dependence → nth-order irreversible decay: dA/dt = -k * A^n
- Rate that changes sign at a specific concentration → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium: terms like k_f*A - k_r or autocatalytic A*(K-A)
- Rate proportional to A*(constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic-type mechanism with a carrying capacity
- Rate with A in denominator → enzyme-like or inhibition mechanism where high concentration suppresses rate
- Explicit time dependence in rate → non-autonomous system such as photolysis with varying light, catalyst deactivation, or externally driven reaction
- Rate as sum of different powers of A → parallel competing reaction pathways each with different molecularity
- Rate that is polynomial in A with alternating signs → complex mechanism with both production and consumption channels
- Half-integer power of A → surface-catalyzed or radical chain mechanism where dissociation steps produce fractional orders
